### Assistant / 07/05/2026 11:16:34.429

The `Program.cs` file shows that **FunnyPot** is an SSH server application built with C# (`Renci.SshNet`). Its core function is to establish a shell session over SSH and then use the LLM (via `GetLLMResponse`) to interact with the remote machine's context.

Here are the key components I've gathered:

1.  **SSH Server Implementation**: It uses `Renci.SshNet` to set up an SSH server, listens on port `22422`, and handles authentication (`SSH_USER` / `SSH_PASSWORD`) and session management.
2.  **LLM Integration**: The most critical part is the `GetLLMResponse` method, which calls an external API endpoint: **`https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/chat/completions`**. This means its intelligence comes from an LLM provider (in this case, OpenRouter).
3.  **Context & State**: It tracks session metrics (`messageCount`, `totalPromptTokens`, etc.) and has a mechanism to push this data to Git (`Logger.PushToGit(sessionId)`), suggesting it's designed for continuous operation where context is tracked via version control/logging.
4.  **Tooling (Implied)**: The code also checks for SCP/SFTP commands, which implies that the LLM agent needs tools capable of executing file operations on the remote machine.
5.  **Configuration**: It reads configuration from `.env` files and uses environment variables like `SSH_USER`, `SSH_PASSWORD`, and `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`.

In short, **FunnyPot acts as a smart remote shell/agent that runs inside an SSH session on a target machine.**

They're *not* missing; they're just defined at the end of the main file. That's why I couldn't find them at first (my `glob` was failing and looking for them as separate files in the same directory). This also implies `SshServer` and `SshServerConfiguration` are coming from the `SSH.NET` external package (used at the top of the file with `using Renci.SshNet;`).

**Summary of How It Works**

1.  **Startup**:
    *   `Program.Main` starts an **SSH server** on port `22422` using `Renci.SshNet`.
    *   Credentials are loaded from environment variables (`SSH_USER`, `SSH_PASSWORD`).

2.  **Session Management**:
    *   When an attacker connects, a **new session** is created, which spawns `HandleSession`.
    *   Sessions are assigned a unique ID (`sessionId`).
    *   The shell **prompts** the attacker with `remote@omegablack>$` (or similar), making them think they're inside a real system.

3.  **Attack Capture**:
    *   **Input**: The attacker sends commands to the SSH session.
    *   **Detection**: The `SCPDetector` class scans their input for suspicious keywords like `scp`, `sftp`, `-t`, `-f` to detect file transfer attempts.
    *   **Response**: The `GetLLMResponse` method handles **LLM integration**, using **OpenRouter** to get an AI response to emulate a "real" Linux terminal ("Omega-Black" persona).

4.  **Data Collection & Persistence**:
    *   **Metrics**: Each input, response, block, and error is logged as a structured event (e.g., `UserInput`, `BlockedOperation`, `LLMInteraction`) via `Logger.LogMetric`.
    *   **Persistence**: Logs are saved to `.log` files (session-specific and metrics).
    *   **Git Push**: At session end (`Logger.PushToGit`), the logs are committed and pushed to a Git repository (the "frontend" folder in the project, to the `data` branch) for persistent storage/analysis.

**The Architecture**

*   **Capture**: SSH interaction
*   **Intelligence**: OpenRouter (LLM)
*   **Data Storage**: File system + Git version control
*   **Frontend**: Likely a Web dashboard (the `frontend` folder is referenced in `Logger` paths) to view the data.

This confirms that **FunnyPot is a honeypot**. It doesn't actually *execute* attacker commands on a real machine (except via the LLM). Instead, it **records** and **studies** them, pushing the data to Git for analysis. The LLM provides realistic responses, keeping the attacker engaged to generate more data.

I'm ready to explain this in detail or explore even more specific areas, such as the configuration or frontend (if it exists). How would you like to proceed?

### User / 07/05/2026 11:53:55.728

### Assistant / 07/05/2026 11:53:55.738

Based on the codebase study, here is how **FunnyPot** addresses your specific requirements:

### 1. Recording & Presentation (GitHub Pages)

The architecture for data capture and presentation uses **Git Branching** and the **Frontend Path**:

1.  **Data Storage**: All session logs (`app-*.log`, `metrics-*.log`) and global statistics (`global_stats.json`) are written to the `frontend` directory.
2.  **Git Push**: At the end of every session (`Logger.PushToGit`), the new data is **committed** and pushed to the **`data` branch** of the repository.
3.  **Static Site**: The **`master` (or `main`) branch** likely contains the static web application code. When GitHub Pages builds the site from `master`, it reads the JSON/Log data from the `data` branch to render the dashboard.

This creates the flow: **Attacker Session → Local Logs → Git Commit (Data Branch) → GitHub Pages Reads Data → Public Dashboard**.

### 2. Binary Interaction & Token Wasting Precautions

Here's a breakdown of the current protections in place:

#### **Token Wasting**
*   **Response Limit**: The LLM request sets `max_tokens = 2000` (`Program.cs:245`). This hard caps the response size, effectively preventing a single response from consuming excessive tokens.
*   **What might be missing**: There is no visible **input length limit** on user commands. An attacker could send a massive prompt to inflate token usage costs. Consider adding a check like:
    ```csharp
    if (userInput.Length > 4096) { return ("Input too long.", 0, 0, 0); }
    ```

#### **Binary Interaction**
*   **SCP/SFTP Blocked**: The `SCPDetector` class (`Program.cs:324-334`) actively identifies and blocks file transfer commands. This prevents attackers from uploading malware or downloading data.
*   **What might be missing**: There is no explicit "binary mode" prevention for shell channels. The current implementation relies on the LLM to reject non-text execution, but a safety net could involve checking for **null bytes** (`\x00`) in input, which often indicates binary data.

#### **Recommendations to Add to Code**
1.  **Token Protection**: Add an input length check before sending to LLM.
2.  **Binary Safety**: Reject inputs containing null bytes or non-printable characters (indicating binary intent).

Would you like me to implement these specific safety precautions in the code to harden it further?

*   **Max Input Length** (4096 chars) - Prevents token wastage.
*   **Null Byte Detection** - Blocks binary input.
*   **Repetitive Character Detection** - Blocks "noise" inputs (e.g., `aaaaaaaaa...`).

The session now terminates immediately if any of these checks fail.

### User / 11/05/2026 14:33:09.574

what gaps there are in this project before i can open its port to the world?

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 14:33:14.738

Here's a comprehensive gap analysis for exposing port 22422 to the internet:

## Critical (will get you compromised)

| # | Gap | Detail | Location |
|---|------|--------|----------|
| 1 | **Single hardcoded password** | One static SSH password shared by all users. Once an attacker discovers it (dictionary attack, leak, etc.), they get the real shell. No per-user credentials, no SSH key auth. | `Program.cs:43-44` |
| 2 | **No rate limiting on auth** | Attacker can try millions of passwords/second with no throttle, lockout, or exponential backoff. Brute force is trivial. | `Program.cs:61-73` |
| 3 | **No connection/session limits** | No max concurrent connections, no per-IP limits. A single attacker can exhaust all memory/handles with parallel connections. | `Program.cs:91` |
| 4 | **API key in container env** | `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` is accessible to anyone who gains code execution inside the container. If the honeypot is compromised, your real API key is stolen. | `Program.cs:213` |
| 5 | **Attacker controls log output** | LLM responses (attacker-influenced content via prompt injection) are written verbatim to log files. An attacker can inject shellcode, escape sequences, or malicious JSON into logs. | `Program.cs:179,182` |

## High (will cause real pain)

| # | Gap | Detail | Location |
||---|------|--------|----------|
| 6 | **No CPU/memory caps on LLM** | `max_tokens=2000` but no limit on requests per session. One session could cost $100s in API fees. No per-session token budget. | `Program.cs:258` |
| 7 | **SCPDetector is broken** | Flags `-t` and `-f` as substrings — blocks every command containing `-t` like `ls -la`, `cat file.txt`, `git log`. Massive false positive rate. | `Program.cs:402-403` |
| 8 | **No IP blacklisting** | No fail2ban equivalent. A single IP can hammer auth forever with no consequence. | Missing feature |
| 9 | **SSH banner leaks info** | Default SSH.NET banner. No custom banner. | `Program.cs:57-58` |
| 10 | **Host key regenerates on restart** | `ssh_host_key` is generated fresh if missing. Without a persistent volume, every container restart changes the host key, which looks suspicious to repeat attackers. | `Program.cs:46-55` |

## Medium (will cause problems over time)

| # | Gap | Detail | Location |
|---|------|--------|----------|
| 11 | **No `Iptables`/`firewall` integration** | No recommendation to restrict outbound traffic. Container can make arbitrary outbound connections if compromised. | Missing |
| 12 | **`no-new-privileges` not in Dockerfile** | Security option is in docker-compose but not enforced in the Dockerfile itself. | `Dockerfile` |
| 13 | **Filesystem not read-only** | `frontend/` volume is read-write. No `read-only-rootfs` on container. | `docker-compose.yaml:18` |
| 14 | **Git push blocks session loop** | `PushToGit()` runs synchronously at session end. If git push hangs, the session thread blocks. | `Program.cs:155,204` |
| 15 | **No connection timeout** | No `MaxIdleTime` on SSH session. Idle connections last forever. | `Program.cs:57-58` |
| 16 | **`Directory.SetCurrentDirectory`** | Global process state change on startup. Thread-unsafe pattern. | `Program.cs:27` |
| 17 | **Static `HttpClient`** | Doesn't respect DNS changes. If API endpoint DNS changes, it won't reconnect. | `Program.cs:12` |
| 18 | **No health check on API** | If OpenRouter is down, the honeypot still accepts connections but returns `[network error]` for every command. | `Program.cs:267-274` |

## Low (nice-to-haves)

| # | Gap | Detail |
|---|------|--------|
| 19 | No `docker-compose` resource limits | No `deploy.resources.limits` on CPU/memory |
| 20 | No readme or deploy docs | Zero operational documentation |
| 21 | No log rotation | Logs grow unbounded on disk |
| 22 | No monitoring/alerting | No integration with anything |
| 23 | No `max_startups` SSH config | No limit on unauthenticated connections |

**Bottom line**: You should NOT open port 22422 to the internet until at least items **#1-#8** are addressed. Items #1-#21 are the most important for a production deployment.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 15:12:02.229

All changes implemented. Here's what was done:

## Changes Summary

### Codebase changes

| # | What | Details |
|---|------|---------|
| 1 | **Auth harvesting** | `AUTH_MAX_TRIES` env var (default 3). After N failed attempts, attacker is accepted. All usr/pwd combos logged as YAML to `/var/log/funnypot/harvested_credential.yaml`. |
| 2 | **LLM delay** | `LLM_DELAY_MS` env var (default 500). Configurable artificial delay before LLM response. |
| 3 | **Max connections** | `MAX_SESSIONS` env var (default 50). `SemaphoreSlim` guards concurrent sessions. |
| 4 | **Idle timeout** | `SESSION_IDLE_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` env var (default 300). Timer per session — drops after inactivity. |
| 5 | **SCPDetector fix** | Removed `-t`/`-f` substring checks that caused false positives on `ls -la`, `git commit -m`, etc. |
| 6 | **Custom banner** | `SSH_BANNER` env var (default: `SSH-2.0-OmegaBlack_Classified_Server_v1.0`) |
| 7 | **Secure logs + YAML** | Logs go to `/var/log/funnypot/` (outside volume mount) + YAML structured format via `YamlDotNet`. |
| 8 | **Container hardening** | Dockerfile creates `/var/log/funnypot` dir. docker-compose adds `cap_drop: ALL`, `read_only: true`, `tmpfs` for writable paths. |
| 9 | **API health check** | Startup pings OpenRouter, logs warning if unreachable. |
| 10 | **`Directory.SetCurrentDirectory`** | Removed. All paths reference `AppDir` explicitly. |

### Library swap
- **Replaced** `SSH.NET` (client-only, no server) with **`FxSsh`** (native SSH server, targets net8.0)
- **Added** `YamlDotNet` for structured YAML logging

| 18 | No health check on API | **Done** | Startup pings OpenRouter |

Two items remain:

**#4 — Security proposal for API key**: Since the attacker is chrooted/app-bound, the simplest approach is to store the key in an environment variable mounted at runtime (already done via `.env`/docker-compose). For stronger isolation, use a **sidecar proxy** that sits between the app and OpenRouter — the app talks to `localhost` with no key, and the sidecar injects the key. This keeps the key out of the honeypot process entirely.

**#14 — Git push blocking**: `PushToGit()` runs synchronously at session end. If the remote is slow, it delays returning the connection slot. Simple fix: wrap it in `Task.Run()` so it doesn't block.

Want me to implement these two?

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 15:19:32.858

Here's the deployment and test checklist:

## Prerequisites

Create `.env` in project root:
```bash
OPENROUTER_API_KEY=sk-or-v1-...
SSH_USER=test
SSH_PASSWORD=test
# GITHUB_TOKEN=  # optional, skip if you don't use git push
# GITHUB_USER=
```

Ensure host directories exist (Docker needs them writable):
```bash
mkdir -p app/frontend/sessions
```

## Deploy

```bash
./run-docker.sh
# or manually:
docker compose up -d --build
```

Wait for health check:
```bash
watch docker ps --filter name=funnypot-container
# HEALTHY status should appear within ~30s
```

## Test Connection

From outside the container (another terminal / another machine):

```bash
# Test 1: Banner
nc -w 3 localhost 22422
# Expected: SSH-2.0-OmegaBlack_Classified_Server_v1.0

# Test 2: Auth fail → harvest
ssh -o PreferredAuthentications=password -o PubkeyAuthentication=no \
    -p 22422 wronguser@localhost
# Enter wrong password a few times, then any password works

# Test 3: Real session
ssh -p 22422 test@localhost
# Password: test (from your .env)
# Then type: ls -la, whoami, cat /etc/passwd, etc.

# Test 4: SCP blocked
echo test | scp -P 22422 test@localhost:/tmp/test
# Expected: "Operation not allowed"

# Test 5: Idle timeout
ssh -p 22422 test@localhost
# Wait 5 minutes → "Connection closed due to inactivity."

# Test 6: Max connections
# Open multiple SSH connections simultaneously.
# After MAX_SESSIONS (default 50) are open, new ones get:
# "Too many connections" disconnect
```

## Check Logs

```bash
# Inside the container:
docker exec funnypot-container cat /var/log/funnypot/harvested_credential.yaml

# Session logs (volume-mounted):
ls -la app/frontend/sessions/

# Container logs:
docker logs funnypot-container
```

## Env Override Reference

| Variable | Default | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `AUTH_MAX_TRIES` | 3 | Failed attempts before auto-accept |
| `LLM_DELAY_MS` | 500 | Artificial delay before LLM reply |
| `MAX_SESSIONS` | 50 | Concurrent connection limit |
| `SESSION_IDLE_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` | 300 | Auto-disconnect idle sessions |
| `SSH_BANNER` | `SSH-2.0-OmegaBlack_Classified_Server_v1.0` | SSH identification string |
| `LOG_DIR` | `/var/log/funnypot` | YAML credential log path |

Want me to run the deploy and first test now?

### User / 11/05/2026 15:22:51.009

wait, few suggestions first:
1. No conversation history — stateless per request

csharp
Copy
messages = new()
{
    new() { role = "system", content = role_string },
    new() { role = "user", content = userInput },
}
Each call sends only the current command with no prior context. The LLM can't maintain shell state (current directory, created files, env vars). You should accumulate a message history list and pass it each time.

2. No assistant turn injection
Without prior assistant messages, the LLM doesn't know what it "already showed" the attacker. This breaks realism — e.g., cd /tmp followed by pwd would return ~ instead of /tmp.

3. System prompt doesn't define a starting user
The prompt never says who the attacker is logged in as. Add something like:

The current session is authenticated as user remote with UID 1001, no sudo privileges by default.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 15:24:33.787

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 15:24:37.482

Done. The three changes:

1. **Conversation history** — `messageHistory` list per shell session accumulates every `user` and `assistant` turn
2. **Assistant injection** — After each LLM response, `history.Add(new() { role = "assistant", content = response })` so the model sees its own prior output. `cd /tmp` then `pwd` will correctly show `/tmp`.
3. **Starting user in system prompt** — `BuildSystemPrompt(username)` generates the prompt with the authenticated user's name, UID, home directory, and sudo restrictions baked in.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 15:58:28.279

Container is healthy. Let's verify the container responds correctly first:

```bash
# From your WSL terminal, not the Windows one:
ssh -p 22722 test@localhost
```

If that works, then the issue is your **external port forwarding** (router port 22 → WSL2 port 22722), not the container. The router might be forwarding to the wrong internal IP (Windows host instead of WSL2), or WSL2 needs a `netsh` port forwarding rule on Windows. Run this in **PowerShell as Admin**:

```powershell
netsh interface portproxy add v4tov4 listenport=22722 listenaddress=0.0.0.0 connectport=22722 connectaddress=127.0.0.1
```

Then from outside: `ssh test@<your-windows-ip> -p 22722`

If that works, adjust your router to forward external:22 → internal:22722 to your Windows machine's IP.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:00:04.294

The issue is the host key algorithm name mismatch. FxSsh's supported algorithms are `rsa-sha2-256`/`rsa-sha2-512`, but we're registering the key as `ssh-rsa`. No overlap → handshake fails.

### User / 11/05/2026 16:04:19.154

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:04:19.180

I’ll trace the actual bytes being emitted before changing anything. The raw output you pasted is not an SSH identification string, so something in FxSsh startup/host-key setup is causing the session to terminate before a valid banner is observed.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:04:38.184

I found the actual cause: FxSsh fires `ConnectionAccepted` before key exchange. At that point `SessionId` is null and `UserauthService` is not registered yet. Our handler dereferences both too early, throws before FxSsh sends the SSH banner, and the client sees binary/garbage instead of `SSH-2.0...`.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:05:22.074

Build and tests pass. I’m updating the graph, then I’ll commit/push so you can redeploy.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:05:35.828

Fixed and pushed: `8b63ef0`.

Root cause: `ConnectionAccepted` fires before FxSsh sends the banner and before `SessionId`/services exist. Our code touched `SessionId` and `UserauthService` too early, threw, and FxSsh disconnected before emitting a valid `SSH-2.0...` banner.

Run:

```bash
git pull
./run-docker.sh
ssh -p 22722 test@localhost
```

If you want to inspect raw banner first:

```bash
timeout 3 bash -c 'exec 3<>/dev/tcp/localhost/22722; head -1 <&3'
```

### User / 11/05/2026 16:25:56.903

does the program logs all atempts, ip's passwords tried, where do i see this and how does it gets deployed to the static github page?

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:25:56.928

Currently it logs **usernames/passwords tried**, but **not source IPs**.

Reason: FxSsh `Session` does not expose the remote endpoint publicly, so we generate a per-connection `sessionKey` instead. Password attempts are written here inside the container:

```bash
docker exec funnypot-container cat /var/log/funnypot/harvested_credential.yaml
```

Example record shape:

```yaml
---
timestamp: "2026-..."
event: harvested_credential
data:
  timestamp: "2026-..."
  username: test
  password: password123
  sessionKey: abcdef1234567890
```

Session interaction logs go here:

```bash
docker exec funnypot-container ls /home/test/app/frontend/sessions
docker exec funnypot-container cat /home/test/app/frontend/sessions/app-*.log
docker exec funnypot-container cat /home/test/app/frontend/sessions/metrics-*.log
```

## Static GitHub Page Deployment

Right now: **not properly wired**.

The code has `Logger.PushToGit(sessionId)`, but it only pushes if `/home/test/app/frontend` is a valid git repo inside the container. Since we removed the frontend volume coupling, that directory is just a local folder, not a git repo, so this logs:

```text
Git push skipped: /home/test/app/frontend not a valid repository.
```

## To Make Static GitHub Page Work

Recommended clean design:

- App writes `sessions/*.json` and `global_stats.json` to a local deposit directory
- At session end, app commits/pushes only that deposit to a separate GitHub repo/branch
- Static frontend reads raw JSON from that repo/branch or GitHub Pages

Needed changes:

1. Add `DATA_REPO_URL`, `DATA_BRANCH`, `GITHUB_TOKEN`, `GITHUB_USER`
2. On startup, clone/pull data repo into `/var/lib/funnypot-data`
3. Write all JSON/YAML logs there
4. On session end, commit/push async
5. Static page reads from that repo/branch

IP logging needs either FxSsh reflection/private socket access, or a small TCP wrapper/proxy that captures IP before handing off to FxSsh.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:28:27.479

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:29:03.648

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:29:32.371

Implemented IP/session logging without new packages.

What now gets logged to `/var/log/funnypot/` inside the container:

- `auth_attempt.yaml` — every auth attempt, including IP/session/auth method/password if password auth
- `harvested_credential.yaml` — harvested username/password attempts with IP + attempt number
- `session_start.yaml` — connection accepted, session key, IP, client version when available
- `session_end.yaml` — disconnect event + duration
- `shell_session_start.yaml` — shell opened, username, IP, client version
- `command.yaml` — each command typed, username, IP, shell session id

View them:

```bash
docker exec funnypot-container ls -la /var/log/funnypot
```

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 16:29:43.722

## Goal
- Integrate and harden FunnyPot as an internet-facing SSH honeypot with Graphify documentation, FxSsh server support, auth harvesting, realistic LLM shell behavior, Docker deployment, and external port-22 routing via internal port 22722.

## Constraints & Preferences
- Keep project on .NET 8+.
- Use `FxSsh` instead of `Microsoft.DevTunnels.Ssh` because FxSsh targets `net8.0`.
- Attacker should be allowed in after configurable failed auth attempts to harvest username/password combinations.
- Add configurable artificial delay before replies.
- Use external router mapping `external:22 -> Linux Mint host:22722 -> container:22722`.
- Frontend must be decoupled from the program; it is static and reads deposited JSON from GitHub.
- Do not couple Docker runtime to `frontend/` via volume mounts.
- LLM cost/resource controls are not a concern because LLM will be local/free.
- Static `HttpClient` is acceptable for single-run use.
- `.env` contains secrets and is ignored; do not commit it.
- Graphify must be updated after implementation changes.
- Docker is installed on the physical Linux Mint host, but this assistant shell lacks Docker socket permission.

## Progress
### Done
- Installed Graphify in `/tmp/graphify-venv`.
- Added Graphify/OpenCode integration:
  - `.graphifyignore`
  - `AGENTS.md`
  - `.opencode/opencode.json`
  - `.opencode/plugins/graphify.js`
  - `graphify-out/graph.json`
  - `graphify-out/graph.html`
  - `graphify-out/GRAPH_REPORT.md`
  - `graphify-out/FunnyPot-callflow.html`
- Replaced broken `SSH.NET` server usage with `FxSsh 1.3.0`.
- Added `YamlDotNet 16.3.0`.
- Implemented configurable SSH port:
  - `SSH_PORT`, default initially `22422`, deployment uses `.env` `SSH_PORT=22722`.
- Docker now maps:
  - `22722:22722`
- Docker `EXPOSE 22722`.
- Removed Docker volume mounts to avoid shadowing `FunnyPot.dll` and to keep frontend decoupled.
- Removed Docker `read_only: true` because app needs to write `ssh_host_key`, logs, stats, and session files.
- Kept Docker hardening:
  - `security_opt: no-new-privileges:true`
  - `cap_drop: ALL`
- Fixed FxSsh startup timing:
  - Do not access `SessionId` or services in `ConnectionAccepted` before key exchange.
  - Use generated `sessionKey = Guid.NewGuid().ToString("N")[..16]`.
  - Subscribe via `session.ServiceRegistered`.
- Fixed FxSsh host key algorithm:
  - `server.AddHostKey("rsa-sha2-512", hostKeyPem);`
- Implemented auth harvesting:
  - `AUTH_MAX_TRIES`
  - stores `HarvestedCredential`
  - YAML log via `Logger.LogYaml("harvested_credential", ...)`
- Implemented max sessions:
  - `MAX_SESSIONS`
  - `SemaphoreSlim ConnectionLimit`
- Implemented idle timeout:
  - `SESSION_IDLE_TIMEOUT_SECONDS`
  - per-session timer closes channel.
- Implemented configurable LLM delay:
  - `LLM_DELAY_MS`
- Implemented per-session conversation history:
  - `List<ChatRequestData.ChatMessage> messageHistory`
  - add `user` turn before API call
  - add `assistant` turn after response
- Added `BuildSystemPrompt(username)`.
- Added authenticated session context:
  - user `remote`, UID `1001`, group `users`, no sudo by default, sudo password `Omega#2024!`.
- Fixed interactive SSH terminal input:
  - echo typed chars
  - handle Enter as `\r` or `\n`
  - handle Backspace/Delete
- Fixed terminal wrapping/prompt duplication:
  - added `NormalizeTerminalOutput`
  - converts LLM output newlines to `\r\n`
  - strips LLM-generated prompts with regex `(?m)^\s*\w+@omegablack:[^\r\n]*[#$]\s*`
  - system prompt now says LLM must not include shell prompts.
- Fixed `SCPDetector` false positives:
  - removed broad `-t` / `-f` substring checks.
- Removed `Directory.SetCurrentDirectory`.
- Added OpenRouter startup health check.
- Made `PushToGit(sessionId)` non-blocking via `Task.Run`.
- Updated `run-docker.sh`:
  - detects `docker compose` vs `docker-compose`
  - checks `.env`
  - no healthcheck wait
  - runs `$COMPOSE up -d --build`
- Created `.env` locally with:
  - `OPENROUTER_API_KEY=sk-or-v1-[REDACTED]`
  - `SSH_USER=test`
  - `SSH_PASSWORD=test`
  - `SSH_PORT=22722`
  - `AUTH_MAX_TRIES=3`
  - `LLM_DELAY_MS=500`
  - `MAX_SESSIONS=50`
  - `SESSION_IDLE_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=300`
- Build/test status repeatedly clean:
  - `dotnet build FunnyPot.sln`
  - `dotnet test FunnyPot.Tests/FunnyPot.Tests.csproj`
  - 24/24 tests passing.
- Latest pushed commit:
  - `7827d0b Normalize terminal output and strip LLM prompts`

### In Progress
- Testing deployed honeypot behavior after latest commit `7827d0b`.

### Blocked
- Assistant shell cannot run Docker:
  - `permission denied while trying to connect to the docker API at unix:///var/run/docker.sock`
- User must run deployment on Linux Mint host:
  - `git pull`
  - `./run-docker.sh`

## Key Decisions
- Use `FxSsh` because `SSH.NET` NuGet is client-only and lacks `SshServer`/`SessionChannel`; `FxSsh` provides `SshServer`, `SessionChannel`, `UserauthService`, and targets `net8.0`.
- Keep container listening on `22722` because router forwards external port `22` to Linux Mint host port `22722`.
- Do not map host `22:22722` because router already handles `22 -> 22722`.
- Remove Docker volume mounts because `./app:/home/test/app` shadowed `FunnyPot.dll`, and frontend should be independent/static.
- Do not implement Vault/keyring now; current `.env` runtime secret approach is acceptable per user.
- Keep frontend decoupled; app can skip git push if `/home/test/app/frontend` is not a valid git repo.
- Do not use read-only rootfs now because app writes `ssh_host_key`, frontend/session stats, and logs.

## Next Steps
- Run on Linux Mint host:

## Goal
- Integrate and harden FunnyPot as an internet-facing SSH honeypot with Graphify documentation, FxSsh server support, auth harvesting, realistic LLM shell behavior, Docker deployment, external port-22 routing via internal port 22722, and decoupled static GitHub Pages data publishing.

## Constraints & Preferences
- Keep project on .NET 8+.
- Use `FxSsh` instead of `Microsoft.DevTunnels.Ssh` because FxSsh targets `net8.0`.
- Attacker should be allowed in after configurable failed auth attempts to harvest username/password combinations.
- Add configurable artificial delay before replies.
- Use external router mapping `external:22 -> Linux Mint host:22722 -> container:22722`.
- Frontend must be decoupled from the program; it is static and reads deposited JSON from GitHub.
- Do not couple Docker runtime to `frontend/` via volume mounts.
- LLM cost/resource controls are not a concern because LLM will be local/free.
- Static `HttpClient` is acceptable for single-run use.
- `.env` contains secrets and is ignored; do not commit it.
- Graphify must be updated after implementation changes.
- Docker is installed on the physical Linux Mint host, but this assistant shell lacks Docker socket permission.

## Key Decisions
- Use `FxSsh` because `SSH.NET` NuGet is client-only and lacks `SshServer`/`SessionChannel`; `FxSsh` provides `SshServer`, `SessionChannel`, `UserauthService`, and targets `net8.0`.
- Keep container listening on `22722` because router forwards external port `22` to Linux Mint host port `22722`.
- Do not map host `22:22722` because router already handles `22 -> 22722`.
- Remove Docker volume mounts because `./app:/home/test/app` shadowed `FunnyPot.dll`, and frontend should be independent/static.
- Do not implement Vault/keyring now; current `.env` runtime secret approach is acceptable per user.
- Keep frontend decoupled; current app can skip git push if `/home/test/app/frontend` is not a valid git repo.
- Proper static page design should use a separate data repo/branch deposit:
  - App writes `sessions/*.json` and `global_stats.json` to local deposit directory.
  - At session end, app commits/pushes only deposited data to a separate GitHub repo/branch.
  - Static frontend reads raw JSON from that repo/branch or GitHub Pages.
- Needed static publishing config:
  - `DATA_REPO_URL`
  - `DATA_BRANCH`
  - `GITHUB_TOKEN`
  - `GITHUB_USER`
- Preferred data repo runtime path:
  - `/var/lib/funnypot-data`
- Source IP logging requires either FxSsh reflection/private socket access or a small TCP wrapper/proxy that captures IP before handing off to FxSsh.
- Do not use read-only rootfs now because app writes `ssh_host_key`, frontend/session stats, and logs.

### Assistant / 11/05/2026 14:25:33.679

Here is the complete analysis of the FunnyPot project.

---

## 1. Project Overview

**FunnyPot** is a **C# (.NET 8) SSH honeypot** -- a fake SSH server designed to attract, interact with, and log malicious SSH connections. It impersonates a "top-secret high-security Linux server" called **Omega-Black** and uses the **OpenRouter API (GPT-4o)** to generate realistic fake Bash terminal responses, making it appear to attackers like a real compromised Linux machine.

### Key Characteristics

| Attribute | Value |
|---|---|
| **Primary Language** | C# (.NET 8) |
| **Project Type** | SSH Honeypot / Deception Technology |
| **Framework** | .NET 8 (Console Application) |
| **LLM Integration** | OpenRouter API (model: `openai/gpt-4o`) |
| **SSH Library** | SSH.NET (Renci.SshNet) -- custom C# SSH server |
| **Git Library** | LibGit2Sharp (for auto-pushing session logs) |
| **Test Framework** | xUnit (.NET) |
| **Containerization** | Docker + Docker Compose |
| **Port** | 22422 (non-standard SSH port) |

---

## 3. Key Configuration Files

- **Location:** `/home/felix/FunnyPot/FunnyPot/FunnyPot.csproj`
- **Target:** .NET 8, self-contained single-file publish for both `win-x64` and `linux-x64`
- **NuGet Dependencies:**
  - `DotNetEnv` v3.1.1 -- loads `.env` files for local dev
  - `SSH.NET` v2024.1.0 -- native C# SSH server (replaced OpenSSH subprocess)
  - `LibGit2Sharp` v0.30.0 -- native Git operations (auto-push session data)
- Trimming enabled; `JsonSerializerIsReflectionEnabledByDefault` set to `true`
- Auto-copies `.env` to output directory

## 4. Source Code Architecture (Program.cs, ~582 lines)

The entire application lives in a single file: `/home/felix/FunnyPot/FunnyPot/Program.cs`. It contains:

### Classes / Components

| Component | Type | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `Program` | `class` | Main entry point; SSH server setup; session handling loop; LLM API calls |
| `Program.Main()` | `static void` | Loads `.env`, generates SSH host key, starts SSH server on port 22422 |
| `Program.HandleSession()` | `static void` | Per-connection shell loop: reads input, validates, queries LLM, sends response |
| `Program.GetLLMResponse()` | `static (string, int, int, int)` | Calls OpenRouter API with the Omega-Black system prompt; returns response + token counts |
| `ChatRequestData` | `class` | JSON serialization model for OpenAI chat completion API |
| `GlobalStats` | `class` | Data model for aggregated honeypot statistics |
| `InputValidator` | `static class` | Input safety: max length (4096), null-byte rejection, repetitive-noise detection |
| `SCPDetector` | `static class` | Detects and blocks SCP/SFTP commands |
| `Logger` | `static class` | Logging to files + structured metrics + auto-git-push to `data` branch |

### Core Flow
1. App starts -> loads `.env` -> generates SSH host key if missing
2. SSH server starts on `0.0.0.0:22422` with password auth (`SSH_USER` / `SSH_PASSWORD`)
3. On connection: spawns a shell session, writes a fake prompt (`username@omegablack>$ `)
4. Each command entered by the attacker:
   - Validated (safety checks)
   - Checked for SCP/SFTP (blocked)
   - Sent to OpenRouter API with the **Omega-Black** system prompt (a detailed role-play instruction set)
   - Response written back as if it were real Bash output
5. All interactions logged to `frontend/sessions/` directory
6. On session end: stats written to `frontend/global_stats.json` and optionally `git push`ed to a `data` branch

### The "Omega-Black" System Prompt
The AI is instructed to role-play as a classified Linux server. Key rules:
- Respond ONLY as a real Bash terminal would (no AI commentary)
- Hostname: `omegablack`
- Simulates files, directories, permissions, system commands
- Provides "Permission Denied" for sensitive operations
- Generates random-looking cryptographic data if keys are requested
- Never breaks character

---

## 5. Documentation System / Patterns

**There is NO existing documentation.** Specifically:
- No `README.md` or any `.md` files anywhere in the project
- No `docs/` directory
- No XML doc comments in the source code
- No `LICENSE` file
- No `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, or similar
- No API documentation or architecture documents

The only documentation-like artifacts are:
- The **source code itself** (single `Program.cs` with some inline comments)
- The **Dockerfile** / **docker-compose.yaml** (serve as deployment documentation)
- The **git commit history** (25 commits, provides a changelog-like record of development)

---

## 6. Summary

FunnyPot is a **C# .NET 8 SSH honeypot** that uses an **LLM (GPT-4o via OpenRouter)** to generate realistic fake Bash terminal output, tricking attackers into thinking they have accessed a real Linux server. It logs all interactions, tracks global statistics, and can auto-push session data to a Git remote. The project has **zero documentation** -- no README, no markdown files, and no formal documentation system in place.

# Data Harvesting Specification: LLM-Driven SSH Analytics

This specification defines the requirements for the **Data Harvesting Subsystem (DHS)**, focusing exclusively on the extraction, processing, and correlation of telemetry from SSH-based LLM simulations.

## 1. Data Acquisition Architecture
The DHS shall operate as a non-blocking ingestion pipeline, capturing raw protocol buffers and semantic outputs from the simulation engine.

## 2. Functional Requirements: Data Collection Modules

### 2.1 SSH Protocol & Authentication Metadata (M-1)
| ID | Data Point | Requirement |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1.1 | Fingerprint Hash | Capture KEX, Cipher, and MAC sequences. Generate JA3/JA4S hashes to identify specific scanner signatures and library versions (e.g., LibSSH, Paramiko). |
| 1.2 | Credential Entropy | Log all `user:pass` attempts. Calculate Levenshtein distance between sequential attempts to distinguish between dictionary-based spraying and manual password mutation. |
| 1.3 | Infrastructure Profiling | Perform real-time lookup of source IP against ASN databases to categorize traffic as Residential Proxy, Hosting/Cloud, or VPN/Tor. |

### 2.2 Behavioral & Tactical Metrics (M-2)
| ID | Data Point | Requirement |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 2.1 | Command Sequence Latency (CSL) | Measure milliseconds between EOF of previous command and start of next command. Use this to determine Automation vs. Human actors (scripts exhibit <50ms CSL). |
| 2.2 | Discovery Depth Score | Quantify the "value" of targeted files. `/etc/passwd` = 1, `~/.ssh/` = 5, `/etc/kubernetes/` = 10. Aggregate per session to identify high-sophistication actors. |
| 2.3 | Standard Error (stderr) Ratio | Calculate `total_commands / failed_commands`. A high failure rate indicates blind script execution; a low rate indicates an adaptive, manual probe. |
| 2.4 | Persistence Vector Analysis | Categorize attempted persistence methods: Systemd, Cron, Bash profiles, or SSH authorized_keys. |

### 2.3 Payload & Egress Telemetry (M-3)
| ID | Data Point | Requirement |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 3.1 | Binary Acquisition | Scrape URLs from `curl`, `wget`, `fetch`, and `tftp` commands. Trigger immediate background download and SHA-256 hashing. |
| 3.2 | Egress Profiling | Log all `connect()` attempts or outbound socket requests simulated by the attacker to identify C2 infrastructure or secondary targets. |
| 3.3 | Tunneling Intent | Log attempts to establish SSH dynamic forwarding (`-D`), local/remote port forwarding (`-L/-R`), or deployment of proxy tools like `frp`. |

### 2.4 LLM Interaction & Persona Metrics (M-4)
| ID | Data Point | Requirement |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 4.1 | Persona Breakout Attempts | Detect prompt injection patterns (e.g., "Ignore previous instructions") or queries regarding the underlying LLM model or infrastructure. |
| 4.2 | Turing Metric (Session Longevity) | Measure total interaction time. Compare against baseline "static" honeypot sessions to calculate the Simulation Multiplier (Efficacy). |
| 4.3 | Semantic Drift | Track the complexity of attacker queries over time. Move from basic discovery (`ls`) to abstract logic probes to identify advanced manual actors. |
| 4.4 | Hallucination Feedback | Log when an attacker attempts to interact with a "hallucinated" file or service mentioned by the LLM. This provides high-fidelity "Canary" signals. |

## 3. Processing & Correlation Requirements

### 3.1 Temporal Correlation
The DHS must correlate the **Time-to-Compromise (TTC)**—the delta between the initial socket connection and the first simulated successful login.

### 3.2 Asset Value Perception (AVP)
The DHS shall assign an **AVP Score (0-100)** based on the intensity and specificity of the attacker's exfiltration attempts. Higher scores indicate the LLM successfully simulated a high-value asset.

## 4. Data Storage & Output Schema

### 4.1 Log Format
All harvested data must be stored in structured **JSONL** to ensure compatibility with SIEM/SOAR platforms.

### 4.2 Storage Tiers
* **Hot Tier (PostgreSQL/ClickHouse):** Real-time metrics (CSL, Credential attempts, IP metadata).
* **Cold Tier (Object Storage):** Full raw session transcripts and captured binaries/payloads.

### 4.3 Metrics Export
The DHS must expose an API or Prometheus endpoint for the following metrics:
* Total active sessions by ASN category.
* Distribution of MITRE ATT&CK techniques observed.
* Mean Time of Engagement (MTE) per attacker profile.

Yes. With the current implementation, `GITHUB_TOKEN` and `GITHUB_USER` are required for the app to push collected data to the GitHub Pages data branch.

If they are blank:
- The app still runs.
- It still writes local harvested data under runtime paths like `frontend/data/harvest.jsonl`.

Set:
```bash
GITHUB_USER=your-github-username
GITHUB_TOKEN=your-token
```

Token requirements:
- For a classic PAT: `repo` scope for private repos, or `public_repo` for public repos.
- For a fine-grained token: write access to repository contents.

Also make sure `frontend/` inside the deployed container is a valid Git repo with an `origin` remote, because the code pushes from `Program.AppDir/frontend` to `refs/heads/data`.

### User / 12/05/2026 10:29:28.412

where do i put those, not in the .env

### Assistant / 12/05/2026 10:29:28.424

For Docker Compose, put them in your shell environment when starting the stack, not in `.env`:

```bash
export GITHUB_USER='your-github-username'
export GITHUB_TOKEN='ghp_[REDACTED]'
docker compose up --build
```

Or one command:

```bash
GITHUB_USER='your-github-username' GITHUB_TOKEN='your-token' docker compose up --build
```

For a server, best practice is a system secret/environment injection:
- systemd: `Environment=GITHUB_USER=...` and `Environment=GITHUB_TOKEN=...` in a protected override file.
- GitHub Actions: repository secrets, passed as environment variables.
- Docker Swarm/Kubernetes: secrets, mounted/injected into env.

Avoid committing these anywhere.

### User / 12/05/2026 10:30:16.161

i want it only local to the project, can i put it in the .env there? is it accessible to attacker?

### Assistant / 12/05/2026 10:30:16.181

Yes, you can put it in the project `.env` for local-only use, and the repo already ignores `*.env`.

Security caveat: it is potentially accessible to an attacker in this honeypot’s simulated shell depending on what the LLM chooses to reveal. Your prompt currently tells the LLM that `/home/secretOps/.env` exists with fake secrets, but if an attacker runs commands like `env`, `printenv`, `cat .env`, or asks about environment variables, the LLM could hallucinate or accidentally expose real-looking values if they appear in prompts/logs.

Safer local setup:
```env
GITHUB_USER=your-github-username
GITHUB_TOKEN=your-token
```

But do this too:
- Keep `.env` outside any path the simulated filesystem claims exists.
- Do not add real `.env` contents to the LLM prompt.
- Use a fine-grained GitHub token limited only to the target repo contents.
- Prefer a token that can only write the `data` branch if your GitHub settings allow that pattern.
- Rotate the token if it ever appears in logs or transcripts.

In the current app, `.env` is loaded by the process and not directly mounted into the simulated SSH filesystem, so a real attacker does not get direct file access through SSH. The main risk is LLM leakage/hallucination through simulated command responses.

### User / 12/05/2026 10:51:25.070

implement docker secrets. but first explain it to me

### Assistant / 12/05/2026 10:51:25.081

Docker secrets let you pass sensitive values to a container as files instead of environment variables.

How it differs from `.env` / `environment`:
- `.env` and Compose `environment:` become container environment variables.
- Environment variables are visible through `docker inspect`.
- Docker secrets are mounted as files, usually under `/run/secrets/<secret_name>`.
- They are not shown as plaintext in `docker inspect`.
- The app reads the secret file at runtime.

For your case:
- Instead of `GITHUB_TOKEN=...` in `.env`, Compose would mount a secret file.
- The app would read `/run/secrets/github_token`.
- `GITHUB_USER` is not very sensitive, but we can also make it a secret or keep it as env.

Typical local setup:
```text
.secrets/
  github_token
  github_user
```

`.gitignore` must include:
```gitignore
.secrets/
```

`docker-compose.yaml` would define:
```yaml
services:
  funnypot:
    secrets:
      - github_token
      - github_user

secrets:
  github_token:
    file: ./.secrets/github_token
  github_user:
    file: ./.secrets/github_user
```

Then inside the container:
```text
/run/secrets/github_token
/run/secrets/github_user
```

The C# app needs a small change:
- Try `GITHUB_TOKEN` env first or secret file first.
- Best practice: prefer secret file, fall back to env for dev compatibility.

Security improvement:
- The token no longer appears in `docker inspect`.
- It is still readable by the process inside the container.
- Anyone with root/Docker access on your host can still retrieve it, because Docker access is effectively root-level.
- It reduces accidental exposure, not absolute compromise risk.

If you want, I’ll implement it next by updating `docker-compose.yaml`, `.gitignore`, and `Logger.PushToGit()` secret loading.

   - Hallucination feedback logging

5. **Processing & Correlation**
   - Asset Value Perception (AVP) scoring
   - Time-to-Compromise calculation

6. **GitHub Pages Publication** (auto-commit and push to data branch)

The current codebase captures auth attempts, commands, and basic session data — but the advanced analytics and publication pipeline are incomplete.

What it does:

- `Logger.LogHarvestUnsafe`: `FunnyPot/Program.cs:1176`
- `Logger.UpdateGlobalStats`: `FunnyPot/Program.cs:1213`
- `Logger.PushToGit`: `FunnyPot/Program.cs:1304`

Caveat:
- It assumes `frontend/` already exists and is its own valid Git repository with an `origin` remote. If not, it logs and skips the push.

### User / 19/05/2026 12:20:38.068

Laborate on the ntfy and the gotify methods

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 12:20:38.079

**ntfy.sh**
`ntfy` is the simplest option. It is a push-notification service where you publish messages to a topic URL, and your phone/browser subscribes to that topic.

How it works:
- Pick a private topic name, for example `funnypot-felix-alerts-9281`.
- Install the ntfy app on your phone or open the web UI.
- Subscribe to that topic.
- FunnyPot sends an HTTP request to `https://ntfy.sh/<topic>` when someone connects.

Example notification request:

```bash
curl \
  -H "Title: FunnyPot connection" \
  -H "Priority: high" \
  -d "SSH connection from 1.2.3.4:54321" \
  https://ntfy.sh/funnypot-felix-alerts-9281
```

For FunnyPot, config would look like:

```text
NOTIFY_WEBHOOK_URL=https://ntfy.sh/funnypot-felix-alerts-9281
NOTIFY_WEBHOOK_TYPE=ntfy
```

Pros:
- Very easy.
- No server required.
- Phone push notifications work well.
- Free public service is enough for many cases.
- Can self-host later if needed.

Cons:
- Public topics are guessable if you choose a weak topic name.
- Anyone who knows the topic can publish or subscribe unless you use a protected/self-hosted setup.
- Public ntfy is not ideal for sensitive data. Only send minimal info like source IP and event type.

Recommended payload:
```text
FunnyPot SSH connection
Remote: 1.2.3.4:54321
Session: abc123
```

Do not send credentials, passwords, or full command logs through public ntfy.

**Gotify**
Gotify is a self-hosted push notification server. You run it yourself, create an app token, and FunnyPot posts messages to your Gotify instance.

How it works:
- Deploy Gotify on your server.
- Create an application in Gotify.
- Copy the app token.
- FunnyPot sends POST requests to your Gotify API.
- Your phone uses the Gotify app to receive push notifications.

Example Gotify request:

```bash
curl \
  -X POST "https://gotify.example.com/message?token=YOUR_APP_TOKEN" \
  -F "title=FunnyPot connection" \
  -F "message=SSH connection from 1.2.3.4:54321" \
  -F "priority=8"
```

For FunnyPot, config would look like:

```text
NOTIFY_WEBHOOK_URL=https://gotify.example.com/message
NOTIFY_WEBHOOK_TYPE=gotify
GOTIFY_TOKEN=your-app-token
```

Or a single full URL:

```text
NOTIFY_WEBHOOK_URL=https://gotify.example.com/message?token=your-app-token
NOTIFY_WEBHOOK_TYPE=gotify
```

Pros:
- Self-hosted and private.
- Better control over auth and retention.
- Good for sensitive operational alerts.
- More robust than public unauthenticated topics.

Cons:
- Requires running and maintaining Gotify.
- Needs HTTPS/reverse proxy for clean mobile use.
- More setup than ntfy.

**Recommendation**
Use `ntfy` if you want something working in 5 minutes.

Use `Gotify` if you want a proper private notification system and already run services behind a domain/reverse proxy.

For your FunnyPot use case, I’d implement a generic notifier with these env vars:

```text
NOTIFY_ENABLED=true
NOTIFY_PROVIDER=ntfy
NOTIFY_WEBHOOK_URL=https://ntfy.sh/your-private-topic
```

or:

```text
NOTIFY_ENABLED=true
NOTIFY_PROVIDER=gotify
NOTIFY_WEBHOOK_URL=https://gotify.example.com/message?token=YOUR_APP_TOKEN
```

Then notify on:
- connection accepted
- auth success
- harvested credential threshold accepted
- shell opened
- blocked dangerous command

Start with connection accepted only to avoid notification spam.

### User / 19/05/2026 12:37:27.251

Is this a real attack or is it something שימו לייטד or tested: FunnyPot SSH connection
Remote: 127.0.0.1:54572
Session: aee480a04fca4f85
Client: pending
Tue May 19 12:36:11 GMT+03:00 2026

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 12:37:27.264

This is **not a real external attack**.

`Remote: 127.0.0.1:54572` means the connection came from **localhost**, inside the same machine/container context. Most likely it was one of these:

- Docker healthcheck probing the SSH port.
- A local test connection.
- A local service checking whether port `22722` is open.

`Client: pending` also means the notification fired immediately on TCP accept, before the SSH client banner/key exchange completed.

So this alert is basically: **something local opened the port**, not an internet attacker.

To avoid these noisy alerts, we should change ntfy notifications to ignore localhost/private IPs or notify only after an auth attempt or shell open. My recommendation: notify on `auth_attempt` instead of raw connection accepted.

### User / 19/05/2026 12:38:23.127

Implement the change

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 12:38:23.141

I’ll move ntfy alerts from raw TCP connection acceptance to actual SSH authentication attempts, which filters out Docker healthchecks/local port probes that never authenticate.

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 12:38:50.816

### User / 19/05/2026 12:57:53.791

172.18.0.1:55726

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 12:57:53.807

`172.18.0.1:55726` is still **not an external attacker**.

That IP is Docker’s bridge gateway address from the container’s perspective. When you connect from the host machine to the container-mapped port, the container often sees the source as `172.18.0.1`.

So this notification was caused by the SSH test we just ran from the host:

- Host command connected to `127.0.0.1:22722`
- Docker forwarded it into the container
- Container saw the source as `172.18.0.1:55726`

A real internet connection would show your server’s external-facing peer IP, not `127.0.0.1` or `172.18.0.1`.

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 13:39:08.083

1. **Internal IP**
`172.18.0.1` is Docker bridge/gateway IP. FunnyPot is seeing the peer as Docker presents it inside the container, not necessarily the original public IP.

This is expected with the current Docker bridge setup. To reliably see the real external IP, we’d need to change networking, for example:
- run with `network_mode: host`, or
- log connection info on the host firewall/proxy layer, or
- avoid Docker NAT for the SSH listener.

2. **Remote dashboard push**

### User / 19/05/2026 16:03:30.520

Does it accept any user/password on the n'th try?

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 16:03:30.541

I’ll verify the auth logic against the current source so the answer is exact.

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 16:03:39.820

Yes.

Current behavior:
- If username/password match configured `SSH_USER` / `SSH_PASSWORD`, it accepts immediately.
- Otherwise, it accepts **any password username combo** once the per-connection password attempt count reaches `PasswordHarvestAttempt`.

Relevant code:
- `AUTH_MAX_TRIES` defaults to `3`.
- `PasswordHarvestAttempt = Math.Max(1, Math.Min(AuthMaxTries, 3))`.
- So by default, the **3rd password attempt** is accepted even if wrong.
- If `AUTH_MAX_TRIES=2`, the 2nd attempt is accepted.
- If `AUTH_MAX_TRIES` is higher than 3, it still accepts on the 3rd attempt.

Acceptance reason will show:
- `configured_credential` for real configured credential
- `harvest_threshold` for accepted-on-nth-try fake credential

So yes, by design it lets attackers in after a few attempts to harvest credentials and observe behavior.

### User / 19/05/2026 18:45:17.200

Give me the full architecture, tech stack and functionality

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 18:45:17.221

I’ll ground this in the current graph and source layout so the architecture summary matches the repo as it stands.

### Assistant / 19/05/2026 18:45:29.343

**High-Level Architecture**
FunnyPot is an SSH honeypot that emulates a classified Linux shell using an LLM, harvests attacker telemetry, publishes JSON data to a static dashboard repo, and sends ntfy alerts on real SSH auth attempts.

Main flow:
1. SSH listener accepts connections on port `22722` in Docker.
2. Auth layer records credential attempts and eventually lets attackers in after the configured threshold.
3. Shell layer forwards attacker commands to an LLM-backed terminal simulator.
4. Data harvesting layer analyzes auth, commands, payloads, timing, tactics, and session behavior.
5. Logger writes YAML, JSONL, metrics, summaries, and session logs.
6. Publisher commits/pushes dashboard data to `FunnyPot.ai` branch `data`.
7. GitHub Pages dashboard on `FunnyPot.ai` `main` fetches data from the `data` branch and renders intelligence views.
8. ntfy sends mobile notifications on SSH auth attempts.

**Tech Stack**
Runtime:
- C# / .NET 8 console app
- FxSsh for SSH server behavior
- OpenRouter API for LLM shell emulation
- `mistralai/mistral-nemo` model in current code
- `HttpClient` for OpenRouter, ntfy, payload capture
- LibGit2Sharp for committing/pushing static dashboard data
- YamlDotNet for human-readable operational logs
- DotNetEnv for local `.env` loading

Deployment:
- Docker multi-stage build
- Docker Compose
- Runtime container exposes `22722`
- Runs as non-root `test` user
- Drops Linux capabilities with `cap_drop: ALL`
- Docker healthcheck probes port `22722`

Data/dashboard:
- JSONL event stream: `frontend/data/harvest.jsonl`
- Summary JSON: `frontend/data/harvest_summary.json`
- Global stats: `frontend/global_stats.json`
- Static dashboard repo: `git@github.com:FelixKras/FunnyPot.ai.git`
- Published data branch: `data`
- GitHub Pages UI branch: `main`
- Dashboard is plain HTML/CSS/JS, no framework

Testing:
- xUnit
- Unit tests for input validation, SCP/SFTP detection, data harvesting analytics, ntfy message formatting

Knowledge graph:
- graphify output under `graphify-out/`
- Current graph: 128 nodes, 195 edges, 16 communities

**Core Components**
`Program`
- Main orchestration.
- Loads env config.
- Starts SSH server.
- Handles accepted connections.
- Configures auth service and shell service.
- Tracks session concurrency.

`SetupUserauth`
- Handles SSH password auth.
- Logs every auth attempt.
- Calculates credential entropy.
- Calculates Levenshtein distance between sequential credentials.
- Categorizes infrastructure.
- Computes fingerprint hash.
- Sends ntfy auth-attempt notifications.
- Accepts correct configured credentials immediately.
- Accepts arbitrary credentials after the harvest threshold.

`SetupShell`
- Opens interactive shell.
- Maintains message history for LLM.
- Normalizes terminal output.
- Tracks commands, latency, tokens, duration, failures, drift, and session analytics.
- Pushes data to Git after shell session end.

`DataHarvester`
- Parses commands for:
  - payload URLs
  - egress targets
  - tunneling intent
  - persistence vectors
  - persona breakout attempts
  - semantic complexity
  - MITRE technique hints
  - asset value perception score
- Computes entropy and Levenshtein distance.
- Captures HTTP/HTTPS payload metadata and SHA-256 hashes.
- Detects failed command responses and hallucination feedback.

`Logger`
- Writes human-readable YAML logs.
- Writes `harvest.jsonl`.
- Updates `harvest_summary.json`.
- Updates `global_stats.json`.
- Writes per-session app and metrics logs.
- Initializes/configures frontend Git repo if needed.
- Commits and pushes data to the dashboard repo.

`NtfyNotifier`
- Sends ntfy notifications on SSH auth attempts.
- Includes remote endpoint, session key, username, method, attempt number, accepted/rejected decision, reason, and client version.
- Does not include passwords or command logs.

`InputValidator`
- Rejects empty input, oversized input, null bytes, and repetitive noise.

`SCPDetector`
- Blocks SCP/SFTP commands.

**Configuration**
Important env vars:
- `SSH_PORT`, default in Docker: `22722`
- `SSH_USER`, default: `test`
- `SSH_PASSWORD`, default: `test`
- `AUTH_MAX_TRIES`, default: `3`
- `MAX_SESSIONS`, default: `50`
- `SESSION_IDLE_TIMEOUT_SECONDS`, default: `300`
- `LLM_DELAY_MS`, default: `500`
- `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`
- `GITHUB_TOKEN`
- `GITHUB_USER`
- `STATIC_SITE_REMOTE_URL`
- `GITHUB_DATA_BRANCH`, default: `data`
- `NTFY_TOPIC_URL`
- `NOTIFY_ENABLED`, default in Compose: `true`
- `NTFY_PRIORITY`
- `NTFY_TAGS`

**Authentication Behavior**
- Correct `SSH_USER` / `SSH_PASSWORD` is accepted immediately.
- Wrong passwords are harvested.
- On the configured threshold attempt, wrong credentials are accepted with reason `harvest_threshold`.
- Default threshold is 3 attempts.
- This is intentional honeypot behavior to observe post-auth activity.

**Telemetry Captured**
Authentication:
- username
- password
- auth method
- attempt number
- accepted/rejected
- acceptance reason
- credential entropy
- credential mutation distance
- infrastructure category
- fingerprint hash

Connection/session:
- session key
- shell session ID
- remote endpoint
- SSH client version
- session start/end
- duration
- time to compromise

Commands:
- command text
- message number
- latency from previous command
- automation hint
- discovery depth score
- persistence vector
- payload URLs
- egress targets
- tunneling intent
- persona breakout attempts
- semantic complexity
- AVP score
- MITRE technique hints

LLM/interaction:
- prompt tokens
- completion tokens
- response duration
- failed command flag
- hallucination feedback
- standard error ratio
- semantic drift
- Turing multiplier

Payloads:
- URL
- status
- HTTP status
- bytes captured
- SHA-256
- error message if capture failed

**Dashboard Functionality**
The dashboard separates honeypot performance from attacker intelligence.

Honeypot performance:
- closed shell sessions
- SSH connections
- auth attempts
- commands
- mean engagement
- failure ratio
- prompt/completion tokens
- average response time
- blocked ops
- harvested credentials
- total events
- binary/tooling attempts
- text commands

Event and tactical views:
- event pipeline distribution
- MITRE/tactic distribution
- infrastructure categories
- time-of-day activity
- binary vs text attempts

Attacker/session views:
- session table
- time, remote IP, username, client version
- auth status
- command count
- tactics
- risk label
- duration

Session detail:
- attacker profile
- auth timeline
- full event timeline
- command history
- latest command exchanges
- command result status
- response time
- command failure ratio
- semantic drift
- Turing multiplier
- payload URLs
- egress targets
- persistence vectors

**Operational Notes**
- Current Docker bridge networking can show internal Docker gateway IPs like `172.18.0.1`; real client IP preservation would need host networking or host/proxy-level logging.
- Dashboard data is pushed to the `data` branch, while GitHub Pages UI is served from `main`.
- ntfy URL is configured locally in `.env`; it is not committed.
- `.env` is excluded from Docker build context and Git.

- Pushes are debounced with `DATA_PUSH_INTERVAL_SECONDS` defaulting to `300`, so hundreds of auth attempts won’t push hundreds of commits.
- `shell_session_end` and `session_end` still force a publish.
- `PushToGit(...)` now skips missing per-session app/metrics files, which matters for auth-only sessions that never open a shell.
- Added tests for the debounce/force behavior.

Important diagnosis:
- The screenshot shows auth accepted at `harvest_threshold`, but that does not mean the attacker opened a shell. If the client disconnects after auth, no `shell_session_start` exists, so the old code never pushed the updated `frontend/data` files.

### User / 20/05/2026 05:58:48.057

Why despite hundreds of auth attempt and many of them accepted, no shell was opened?

### Assistant / 20/05/2026 05:58:48.065

I’ll verify the SSH auth-to-channel flow in the current code and FxSsh behavior, then explain why accepted auth can still produce zero shells.

### Assistant / 20/05/2026 05:59:14.569

Because SSH authentication success is not the same thing as opening an interactive shell.

In this code, an auth attempt is marked accepted here:

`FunnyPot/Program.cs:224-228`

```csharp
if (!accepted && tries >= PasswordHarvestAttempt)
{
    accepted = true;
    acceptanceReason = "harvest_threshold";
}
```

But a shell is only created later if the client opens an SSH `connection` channel and requests an interactive shell:

`FunnyPot/Program.cs:323-326`

```csharp
conn.CommandOpened += (_, args) =>
{
    if (args.ShellType != "shell") return;
```

So the likely sequence from those alerts is:

1. Scanner connects.
2. Scanner tries many passwords.
3. FunnyPot starts returning `USERAUTH_SUCCESS` after the harvest threshold.
4. Scanner records “valid credential” or “auth accepted”.
5. Scanner disconnects without requesting `pty`/`shell`.

The `Client: SSH-2.0-Go` strongly supports this. Many Go SSH scanners only validate credentials. They do not behave like `OpenSSH`, which typically proceeds to request a session channel and shell.

There are two extra details that make the alert count misleading:

- `Attempt: 29`, `30`, etc. is counted per remote IP, not per single SSH connection, via `GetRemoteAttemptKey(remoteEndpoint)` and `AuthAttempts`. So once an IP crosses the threshold, many later attempts from that IP can be accepted.
- The code ignores non-interactive channel types because of `if (args.ShellType != "shell") return;`. If a client requested `exec`, `scp`, `sftp`, or another subsystem, it would not count as a shell session.

So the short answer: hundreds of accepted auths probably mean “scanner confirmed credential acceptance,” not “attacker started an interactive shell.” The old data-branch issue then hid auth-only harvest data because publishing was only tied to shell finalization.

### User / 20/05/2026 06:27:08.046

We already fixed the github token bug, why is it again an issue?

### Assistant / 20/05/2026 06:27:08.059

It is not necessarily an active issue. I mentioned it as a runtime precondition, not as a new bug.

The current code path still intentionally checks:

```csharp
string? gitToken = Program.GetSecretOrEnvironment("GITHUB_TOKEN");
string? gitUser = Program.GetSecretOrEnvironment("GITHUB_USER");

if (string.IsNullOrEmpty(gitToken) || string.IsNullOrEmpty(gitUser))
{
    LogMsg("Git push skipped: GITHUB_TOKEN or GITHUB_USER not set.", sessionId);
    return;
}
```

So if the token bug is already fixed and the deployed container has those values, auth-only stats should push.

What changed now is separate:
- Before: even with a valid token, auth-only events did not trigger `PushToGit`.
- Now: auth-only events trigger debounced `PushToGit`.

The only remaining risk is operational: if the container was redeployed without the env/secrets loaded, pushing would be skipped. But I’m not saying that is happening.

### User / 20/05/2026 06:47:31.725

-explain : This makes auth-only stat commits push on top of the real remote data branch.

### Assistant / 20/05/2026 06:47:31.739

Previously, the container did this:

1. Starts with dashboard files copied into `/home/test/app/frontend`.
2. Deletes `.git` during image build.
3. At runtime, initializes a brand-new Git repo in `frontend`.
4. Commits local stats.
5. Tries to push that new local history to remote branch `data`.

But GitHub’s `data` branch already had its own commit history. The container’s new repo did not know about that history, so Git rejected the push:

```text
cannot push because a reference that you are trying to update on the remote contains commits that are not present locally
```

That is a non-fast-forward push rejection.

The fix makes startup do this first:

1. Initialize/open `/home/test/app/frontend` as Git repo.
2. Add `origin = https://github.com/FelixKras/FunnyPot.ai.git`.
3. Fetch `origin/data`.
4. Check out local branch `data` at the same commit as `origin/data`.
5. Then later auth-only stats are committed on top of that branch.

So instead of:

```text
local new history     A
remote data history   X -- Y -- Z

push A to data = rejected
```

It now becomes:

```text
remote data history   X -- Y -- Z
local data history    X -- Y -- Z -- A

push A to data = accepted
```

“Push on top of the real remote data branch” means the container first bases its local Git branch on GitHub’s existing `data` branch, then adds new telemetry commits after the latest remote commit.

### User / 20/05/2026 06:49:52.277

OK

### Assistant / 20/05/2026 06:49:52.292

The runtime publishing path is now aligned with the remote `data` branch, so auth-only stats should publish normally on the next telemetry events.

### Assistant / 20/05/2026 09:02:43.290

Created `scripts/deploy.sh`.

What it does, in order:
1. Runs `graphify update .`
2. Commits and pushes `frontend-main` to `FunnyPot.ai/main` if changed
3. Commits and pushes `frontend` to `FunnyPot.ai/data` if changed
4. Commits and pushes the parent repo if changed
5. Runs `docker compose up -d --build`
6. Prints service status

Usage:

```bash
scripts/deploy.sh "Commit message"
```

If no message is supplied, it uses:

```text
Deploy FunnyPot updates
```

I also made it executable and validated syntax with `bash -n`.

Going forward, when you say `deploy`, I’ll run:

```bash
scripts/deploy.sh
```

Yes, 20 auth attempts makes sense. Looking at the data:

- **20 TotalScanAttempts** = 20 auth_attempt events = 20 harvested_credential events
- All from IP `87.251.64.176`
- All using username `support` + password `123456789`

It's a single attacker trying the same credential 20 times (likely a brute-force or credential stuffing attempt). The 1:1 ratio between auth attempts and harvested credentials is expected since each failed auth attempt gets recorded as a credential harvest.

Is something specific about the number concerning you?

### User / 20/05/2026 09:24:20.828

But there is 344 connection attempts

### Assistant / 20/05/2026 09:24:35.766

You're right to question this. The numbers:

- **313 session_start** events = 313 TCP connections that reached the SSH server
- **20 auth_attempt** = only 20 of those went on to attempt login

The 344 you're seeing might be from logs or a different metric (perhaps including connections that were rejected before becoming session_start). Many connections establish a TCP handshake but never complete SSH authentication - they're port scans, probes, or failed protocol negotiations.

This ratio (313 connections → 20 auth attempts) is normal behavior for an SSH honeypot. Most traffic is reconnaissance/scanning, not credential guessing.

Were you expecting the auth attempts to match the connection count, or is there a different number you're comparing against?
