### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:03:03.033

The code uses a session-level `llmCts`, and `FinalizeShell()` cancels it. In the screenshot, the attacker appears to be using SSH `exec`, not an interactive shell, so if the exec channel closes while the command is still resolving, it can cancel the LLM almost immediately.

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:03:10.112

Timed it outside the program.

Results:

- OpenRouter `/models`: `0.24s`
- Unauthenticated `/chat/completions`: `0.04s` with expected `401`
- Authenticated `deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro`, tiny prompt: `4.86s`
- Authenticated attacker-style command with `max_tokens: 2000`: `20.74s`

So you’re right: the external request is not taking more than 30 seconds.

The screenshot shows `generated response / 71ms`, which means FunnyPot is probably not reaching the 30s HTTP timeout. The LLM request is being cancelled almost immediately.

Most likely cause in the code:

- `Program.cs` creates `llmCts` for the shell session.
- `FinalizeShell()` calls `llmCts.Cancel()`.
- `channel.CloseReceived` and `channel.EofReceived` call `FinalizeShell()`.
- For SSH `exec` style commands, the client may send EOF/close quickly after sending the command.
- That cancels the OpenRouter request, producing `[api error] Request cancelled or timed out` in ~70ms.

So the issue is probably session/channel cancellation, not OpenRouter latency.

### User / 29/06/2026 21:05:53.860

in this example the attacker sends two commands both got api error, if he cancelled session for the first, how did he manage sending the second?

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:05:53.886

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:06:10.077

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:06:18.049

The worker itself doesn’t cancel between commands. The only explicit cancellation is `FinalizeShell()`, so for same-session two-command behavior we need logs to see whether the UI session is actually aggregating multiple SSH connections or whether `FinalizeShell` happened before each response.

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:06:26.755

This container does not have the plain text log file, only `events.jsonl`. I’ll query that JSONL for the displayed session/remote to see exact event ordering and session IDs.

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:06:36.100

You’re right to question it. The logs show the exact reason:

- It was one SSH connection/session key.
- But it opened two separate SSH `exec` channels.
- Each command has a different `ShellSessionId`.
- Each `exec` channel sent `EofReceived` almost immediately after the command was submitted.
- FunnyPot handles `EofReceived` by calling `FinalizeShell()`, which cancels `llmCts`.
- The LLM request then returns `[api error] Request cancelled or timed out`.

Example from logs:

```text
shell_session_start ... ShellSessionId=3b12... Event=ExecOpened
command ... cd ~; chattr -ia .ssh; lockr -ia .ssh
shell_session_end ... Event=EofReceived
command_result ... [api error] Request cancelled or timed out

shell_session_start ... ShellSessionId=e554... Event=ExecOpened
command ... echo ssh-rsa ... authorized_keys ...
shell_session_end ... Event=EofReceived
command_result ... [api error] Request cancelled or timed out
```

So the attacker did not need to keep the first shell alive. Their SSH client kept the underlying connection open and opened another `exec` channel for the second command.

My earlier wording was incomplete: it’s not necessarily “client closed the whole SSH session.” It’s “the exec channel sends EOF/close before FunnyPot finishes generating the response,” and FunnyPot currently treats that as a reason to cancel the LLM request.

The fix is likely: don’t cancel LLM generation on `EofReceived` for `exec` channels while command processing is still active. Only cancel on actual channel close/disconnect, or after the response is sent.

### User / 29/06/2026 21:08:25.896

what is the difference between eofreceived and exec and close/disconnect?

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:08:25.904

In SSH these are different layers/events.

`exec`
: A request from the client to run one command on a channel.

Example:

```sh
ssh user@host "uname -a"
```

That opens an SSH connection, opens a channel, sends an `exec` request with `uname -a`, waits for output, then closes.

`EofReceived`
: The client says: “I will not send any more input on this channel.”

It does not necessarily mean:

- the command is done
- the channel is closed
- the SSH connection is closed
- the server should stop producing output

For `exec`, EOF is common. The client sends the command, then sends EOF because stdin is finished. The server should usually continue processing and still send stdout/stderr back.

`CloseReceived`
: The client says: “This channel is closed.”

This is stronger than EOF. After channel close, the server generally cannot send more data on that channel.

`disconnect`
: The whole SSH transport connection ended.

This means all channels on that SSH connection are gone. No more exec requests, shell input, or output.

In your bug:

- Attacker opens an `exec` channel.
- Sends command.
- Sends EOF quickly because no stdin remains.
- FunnyPot treats EOF as session finalization.
- Finalization cancels the LLM request.
- LLM returns `[api error]`.
- The underlying SSH connection can still exist, so attacker opens another `exec` channel.
- Same thing happens again.

Correct behavior: `EofReceived` should stop reading input, not cancel output generation. FunnyPot should keep generating the command response and send it unless the channel is actually closed/disconnected.

### User / 29/06/2026 21:10:29.500

### User / 29/06/2026 21:34:25.841

explain why new exchnges still show api error?????

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:34:25.902

I’ll verify this against the current running container and event ordering, not infer from the screenshot. The key question is whether these new failures are still `EofReceived` or now `CloseReceived`/disconnect/model timeout.

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:34:37.414

The graph report is stale relative to the latest commit, but enough for navigation; I’m checking container event logs around the displayed timestamp and whether the image contains the EOF fix.

### Assistant / 29/06/2026 21:34:50.357

Because these new ones are **not EOF anymore**.

I checked the live container logs for the exact timestamp in your screenshot. The sequence is:

```text
18:32:25.637 shell_session_start Event=ExecOpened
18:32:25.637 command cd ~; chattr -ia .ssh; lockr -ia .ssh
18:32:26.178 shell_session_end Event=CloseReceived
18:32:28.324 command_result [api error] Request cancelled or timed out ResponseDurationMs=540
```

And for the second command:

```text
18:32:31.108 shell_session_start Event=ExecOpened
18:32:31.109 command cd ~ && rm -rf .ssh ...
18:32:31.670 shell_session_end Event=CloseReceived
18:32:33.531 command_result [api error] Request cancelled or timed out ResponseDurationMs=561
```

So the previous fix worked for `EofReceived`, but these clients are now sending **`CloseReceived`** very quickly, around `0.5s` after command submission.

What is happening:

- Attacker opens SSH `exec`.
- Sends command.
- Closes the channel before the LLM finishes.
- FunnyPot receives `CloseReceived`.
- `CloseReceived` calls `FinalizeShell()`.
- `FinalizeShell()` cancels `llmCts`.
- OpenRouter request throws `OperationCanceledException`.
- FunnyPot records `[api error] Request cancelled or timed out`.

This is not OpenRouter taking 30 seconds. It is still local cancellation, now caused by **channel close**, not EOF.

The response durations in the screenshot, `540ms` and `561ms`, match the logs exactly. That is the client/channel closing too early, not model timeout.

The remaining design problem is:

- Ignoring `EofReceived` is safe because EOF only means “no more stdin.”
- Ignoring `CloseReceived` is trickier because close means the SSH channel is gone, so FunnyPot probably cannot send the response back anyway.
- But for the dashboard/logs, we should not label that as `[api error]`; it should be logged as something like `[client closed] Response generation cancelled because SSH channel closed`.

If you want the dashboard to stop showing `[api error]`, the next fix should distinguish **model/API failure** from **client closed before response**.

### User / 30/06/2026 06:30:18.765

Can i in place upgrade to 26?

### Assistant / 30/06/2026 06:30:18.814

Not directly to Linux Mint 26 from this environment.

You’re on `Ubuntu 24.04.4 LTS`, not Mint. Also, as of now Mint 26 is not a normal in-place target from Ubuntu 24.04.

If you mean **Ubuntu 26.04**: you generally should wait until the official upgrade path opens, then use:

```sh
sudo do-release-upgrade
```

If you mean **Linux Mint 26**: Mint upgrades are supported Mint-to-Mint, not Ubuntu-to-Mint in-place. The safe path is backup, fresh install Mint, then restore data.

For this machine right now, I would not attempt a manual in-place conversion.

### User / 30/06/2026 09:02:59.358

Another ques can i logout of desktop manager and stay only with terminal?

### Assistant / 30/06/2026 09:02:59.412

Yes.

If you want to stop the graphical desktop and stay in terminal:

```sh
sudo systemctl isolate multi-user.target
```

To return to graphical desktop later:

```sh
sudo systemctl isolate graphical.target
```

To make terminal-only boot permanent:

```sh
sudo systemctl set-default multi-user.target
```

To make GUI boot default again:

```sh
sudo systemctl set-default graphical.target
```

You can also switch to a TTY without stopping the desktop using:

```text
Ctrl+Alt+F3
```

Return to GUI usually with:

```text
Ctrl+Alt+F2
```

or sometimes `Ctrl+Alt+F1`, depending on the display manager.

### Assistant / 02/07/2026 15:03:04.786

### Assistant / 02/07/2026 15:03:15.305

The command-only behavior is mainly enforced here:

`FunnyPot/Program.cs:1006-1011`

```csharp
return $@"Execute this exact Bash command on Omega-Black and return only the terminal output, with no prompt, no explanation, no markdown, and no parser trace.

Structured input:
- command_kind: {(isChained ? "chained" : "single")}
- execution_note: {chainInstruction}
- output_contract: raw terminal stdout/stderr only; no JSON, no XML, no markdown, no labels.
```

Also reinforced in the system prompt:

`FunnyPot/Program.cs:958-959`

```text
Respond only with the exact text a real Bash terminal would produce, excluding prompts. Do not add extra commentary or explanation outside of what a Linux terminal would provide.
```

And:

`FunnyPot/Program.cs:993-994`

```text
You are not an AI, an LLM, or a language model. You are the Omega-Black server responding purely as a Bash shell.
```

Suggested fix: make the user prompt explicitly ban visible reasoning, while still allowing internal simulation.

```csharp
return $@"Execute this exact Bash command on Omega-Black. Simulate Bash internally, but output only the final visible terminal stdout/stderr.

Do not explain, reason aloud, summarize, label sections, show parser steps, show markdown, or include a shell prompt. If the command produces no visible output, return an empty response.

Structured input:
- command_kind: {(isChained ? "chained" : "single")}
- execution_note: {chainInstruction}
- output_contract: raw terminal stdout/stderr only; no reasoning, no JSON, no XML, no markdown, no labels.
```

I’d keep the existing system prompt, but replace `BuildCommandUserPrompt` lines `1006-1011` with the stronger version above.

### User / 09/07/2026 06:58:38.564

But why was there an api error in the first place, the m3 is paid model

### Assistant / 09/07/2026 06:58:38.640

The API error was from the fallback, not MiniMax M3.

Flow before the latest fix:

1. Primary model: `minimax/minimax-m3`
2. OpenRouter call failed with `403 Key limit exceeded (total limit)` when I tested it directly.
3. App retried fallback: `nvidia/nemotron-3-super-120b-a12b:free`
4. That fallback returned `429 free-models-per-day-high-balance`
5. The app exposed that raw API error in the exchange card.

So even though M3 is paid, the current OpenRouter key/account is at its total spend/key limit, so paid models are blocked too. Then the app fell back to a free model whose daily free quota was exhausted.

What changed now:
- The backend no longer sends raw API errors to attackers/dashboard.
- The exchange card will show which model was attempted via `LlmModel`.
- If M3 fails due to key limit, the card should show `model minimax/minimax-m3` or the fallback model depending on which attempt produced the final result, but the visible response should be local fallback, not `[api error]`.

### User / 09/07/2026 14:11:32.498

Problems, in order of impact

1. No file exclusion — the graph indexed build output. 1,983 of 2,531 nodes (78%) come from obj/ and bin/ files. The top node producers are FunnyPot.deps.json (501 nodes), FunnyPot.Tests.deps.json (413), and project.assets.json (389) — NuGet lock files, each indexed multiple times across Debug/Release/linux-x64 configurations. The backups/ data dumps contributed another 42 nodes. This is the root cause of everything below. Graphify should respect .gitignore (or at minimum hard-exclude obj/, bin/, backups/). That alone would shrink the graph from 2,531 to roughly 500 nodes.

2. The "God Nodes" section is 80% garbage because of it. 8 of the 10 listed "core abstractions" are runtime, .NETCoreApp,Version=v8.0 (listed twice — so there's also no node dedup by label), net8.0, System.Runtime, resources, resource — JSON keys from NuGet manifests, not abstractions. Only CommandResolver and Program belong there.

3. Generic JSON keys become entities. fileVersion exists as 207 separate nodes, assemblyVersion 185, locale 130, dependencies 120. Structural keys of machine-generated JSON shouldn't be graph entities at all.

4. 411 communities for a ~5-source-file project. The noise fragments clustering — cohesion scores run 0.04–0.27, and communities 22 and 23 are literally identical (Debug vs Release copies of the same deps.json). With clean input this would collapse to a few dozen meaningful clusters.

5. Community labeling never executed. .graphify_labels.json contains only placeholder names ("Community 0", "Community 1", …), consistent with the report's "Token cost: 0 input · 0 output". So the ~390-line "Community Hubs (Navigation)" section is a wall of self-referential links with no information. Either the labeling step silently failed/was skipped, or it should be gated so the report omits that section when labels are placeholders.

6. "Surprising Connections" surfaced trivia. Both entries are FakeFileSystem → Dictionary / → object. BCL and primitive types should be excluded from surprise scoring — a connection to Dictionary surprises nobody.

The core extractor and the doc/viz outputs are in good shape — the source-code graph correctly identifies FunnyPot's honeypot architecture. The tool's weakness is entirely in input hygiene and report curation: respect .gitignore, dedupe nodes by label, blacklist generic JSON keys and BCL types, and skip the community-hub section when labels are placeholders. Fix #1 and re-run, and I'd expect the report to go from mostly-noise to genuinely useful.

### User / 09/07/2026 15:46:48.294

‏do you think it's a good idea to add rapify inside the docker so that lam inside the funny pot will in rich the graphici with attacks and exchanges

### Assistant / 09/07/2026 15:46:48.468

I’ll check the newly regenerated graph report first, then answer from the current architecture rather than guessing.

### Assistant / 09/07/2026 15:46:55.542

Short answer: not inside the honeypot container.

Better approach:
- Keep FunnyPot runtime focused on SSH handling, attacker interaction, logging, and pushing telemetry.
- Enrich the graph outside the live honeypot process, as a separate scheduled job or sidecar.
- Feed it sanitized telemetry/events, not raw live container internals.

Why:
- The honeypot must stay lightweight and reliable. Graph enrichment can be CPU/IO heavy and should not affect attacker sessions.
- If graphify/LLM enrichment fails, it should not risk SSH service health.
- The graph is mostly a developer/code knowledge graph right now. Attack/exchange enrichment is a different graph: telemetry graph, not source-code graph.
- Putting it inside Docker also risks mixing runtime data, generated graph output, and source graph concerns again.

What I’d do instead:
1. Keep current `graphify-out/` as source-code architecture graph.
2. Add a separate `attack-graph` generator that reads `events.jsonl`.
3. Produce nodes like `Session`, `RemoteIP`, `Username`, `Command`, `ResponseSource`, `LLMModel`, `MITRETechnique`, `PayloadURL`.
4. Link them by `SessionKey`, `ExchangeId`, `MessageNumber`, timestamps, and MITRE classifications.
5. Run it from host cron/GitHub Action/sidecar after data push, not from the SSH handling path.
6. Publish output to dashboard as static JSON/HTML.

If you mean “let the LLM enrich the graph with attack summaries,” I’d make that async and cached:
- One summary per session.
- One summary per command cluster.
- Never inline during attacker response generation.
- Store results as `attack_graph.json`, not inside `graphify-out/graph.json`.

So: good idea to enrich a graph with attacks and exchanges, bad idea to put that work directly inside the live FunnyPot container/process.
